Short answer:
S1={1.0, 3.5, 6.0, 7.5, 10.0, 10.5}
S2={1.5, 4.0, 4.5, 5.0, 5.5, 6.0}

This covers all the integers N from 1 to 64.

Long answer:
I got stumped by an unnecessary assumption in that all numbers in S1 and S2 needed to be integers.  With that (unnecessary) constraint in mind, I wrote a brute force algorithm that iterated through all the combinations where the maximum element is <= 15.

I used a recursive data structure of the form
def listOfInts(minel: Int, maxel: Int, n: Int, k: Int): Stream[List[Int]] = {
    if (k == n)
      Stream(List())
    else {
      val a = for {
        i <- (minel + 1) to (maxel - (n - k) + 1)
        row <- listOfInts(i, maxel, n, k + 1)
      } yield i :: row
      a.toStream
    }
  }


This gave me two solutions that made covered up to N=57.
S1 = (1, 5, 6, 7, 8, 13)
S2 = (2, 3, 4, 6, 7, 9)
===
S1 = (1, 3, 4, 6, 7, 9)
S2 = (2, 5, 7, 8, 9, 13)

Unsatisfied that the combinatorics prevented me from searching any higher than 15, I searched using a simulated annealing algorithm.  My domain was 12 integers, so a neighbour is just a single number changed by 1.
The objective function I used was the lowest integer not covered by the products.
I later changed the objective function to the number of missing integers between 1 and 58.
This was unsuccessful in finding a solution, and the nature of the algorithm gave me no indication if there was no solution.

I reattempted my objective function in Octave using nonlinear minimization using a successive quadratic programming solver.  The solver allows for constraints, which I coded up as the number of gaps must be 0.  I asked it to maximize N, but it crapped out with an error message that seemed to me that it wasn't happy that it's wasn't in a continuous domain, so I gave up on Octave.

I thought about the math behind the difficulty.  An upper bound on N must be 2+ 3*35 = 107, since you can't spread the products out any further than every 3rd number.  Twin primes pose a challenge.  The only way to get at 30 for example, in between the primes of 29 and 31 would be to do 1*29, 1*31 or factors of 30 itself.

This led me to implement a third effort.  I built a data structure of all the factors of all the numbers.  Like the example of 30 above, to "cover" 30, you could use the factors of 29, 30, or 31.  A solution (S1,S2) is built up recursively, starting from the empty sets S1 and S2, adding a candidate factor from an uncovered number, as shown in my scala code.


// c is the a structure that contains all the pairs of factors for every integer
 def r(c: IndexedSeq[List[(Int, Int)]], S1: Set[Int], S2: Set[Int]): Boolean = {
    if (S1.size > 6 || S2.size > 6)
      false
    else if (c isEmpty) {
      println("Solution found!")
      println(S1.toList.sorted)
      println(S2.toList.sorted)
      true
    } else {
    // Remove all elements that are now covered
    val cParted = c filterNot(x => x exists(y => S1.contains(y._1) && S2.contains(y._2)))
   
// Sort to attempt the most difficult cases first (... some sort of life lesson here)
// i.e. ones with the fewest factors such as in between twin primes
     val cSorted = cParted sortWith (_.length < _.length)
      if (cSorted.isEmpty)
        r(cSorted,S1,S2)
      else
       (cSorted.head filter (ses => r(cSorted.tail, S1 + ses._1, S2 + ses._2))).size > 0
    }
  }

This worked surprisingly well, and returned the aforementioned two previous solutions to N=57 and none others, and a big fat "False" to N=58.  (The False for N=58 is obvious from inspecting the two solutions to N=57, neither of them cover N=58.  All solutions to N must be present for N-1.... I don't think this inductive step can be used to construct an algorithm since there are too many solutions for low N.)

So this left me wondering what the deal was with improving upon N beyond 57.  There were people with asterisks beside their names, so what was I missing?

It's funny, I thought of somehow using Gaussian integers before rationals.  Then maybe I could use irrationals.  You want random pairs to easy multiply to integers, which irrationals don't do so easily, so I ruled them out for now.  Multiplying to form integers is key, since each product would then be able to cover 3 integers: n-1, n and n+1.  If your product is not an integer, you can only cover the two integers: its floor and ceiling.  I thought of how to design an algorithm that searches this new domain of rationals.  How about if I restrict myself to using half integers?  Floating point would have no trouble with them, unlike general rationals, and I could reuse my algorithms with only a few modifications.

I first reused my brute force search, which quickly gave me a solution up to 64.  Then I tried to reuse my solution-centric approach, but it proved too slow to even solve the N=64 case, let alone more.

I'm currently happy with having solved up to N=64, and see no point in refining my algorithm based on half integers.  I suspect a better approach would be to use something like a table of all rationals that can pairwise multiply to all the integers between 1 and say 15... Say k+a/b such that k, a, b are integers, and 1<b<16. and a<b.  I would then sort this table, and create a list of factors for every integer between 1 and N, then run my recursive algorithm shown above.... But even thinking about this approach makes me think there's a much more elegant number theoretic solution that I'm being blind to.

Thanks for another fun puzzle, and I'm looking forward to yours or other readers' solutions.

Chris Shannon

Calgary Canada

https://github.com/krishnanraman/SimulatedAnnealing/blob/master/SimulatedAnnealing.scala

  val (initialTemperature, coolingRate) = (100000.0, 0.0003)

  case class City(x:Int,y:Int)

  def distance(a:City, b:City) = math.sqrt(List((a.x-b.x),(a.y-b.y)).map(x=>x*x).sum)

  def mkTour(tour:Seq[City]) = {
    val (i,j) = ( util.Random.nextInt(tour.size), util.Random.nextInt(tour.size) )
    tour
    .patch(i,Seq(tour(j)),1)
    .patch(j,Seq(tour(i)),1)
  }

  def length(tour:Seq[City]) = tour.foldLeft(0.0,tour.head)((a,b)=>(a._1 + distance(a._2,b),b))._1

 // If the new solution is better, accept it, else compute acceptance probability
  def acceptanceProbability(energies:(Double,Double), temperature:Double) = {
    val diff = energies._1 - energies._2
    if (diff < 0 ) 1.0 else math.exp(diff/temperature)
  }

  def compute( best:Seq[City], temp:Double):Seq[City] = {
    if (temp > 1) {
          val newSolution = mkTour( best )
          val currentEnergy = length(best)
          val neighbourEnergy = length(newSolution)

          // Decide if we should accept the neighbour
          val accept = (acceptanceProbability((currentEnergy, neighbourEnergy), temp) > math.random) &&
                       (length(newSolution) < length(best))
          compute( if (accept) {
                    printf("\nLength: %.2f, Temperature: %.2f", length(newSolution), temp)
                    newSolution
                  } else best, (1-coolingRate)*temp)
    } else best
  }

  def main(args:Array[String]) = {
    val tour = Seq(City(60, 200),
        City(180, 200),
        City(80, 180),
        City(140, 180),
        City(20, 160),
        City(100, 160),
        City(200, 160),
        City(140, 140),
        City(40, 120),
        City(100, 120),
        City(180, 100),
        City(60, 80),
        City(120, 80),
        City(180, 60),
        City(20, 40),
        City(100, 40),
        City(200, 40),
        City(20, 20),
        City(60, 20),
        City(160, 20))

    val best = compute( tour, initialTemperature)
    printf("\nFinal solution distance: %.2f\n",length(best))
    println("Tour: " + best)
  }







  val (initialTemperature, coolingRate) = (100000.0, 0.0003)

  case class City(x:Int,y:Int)

  def createNeighbour((s1,s2): (Set[Int], Set[Int]) = {
val r = if util.Random.nextInt(24)
0 to 11 are subtract
12 to 23 are add
val addOrSubtract = 2*(r/12) - 1

000000,111111,222222,333333...
val set1or2 = r/6 mod 2

val elementInSet = r mod 6

if (set1or2 == 1)
(s1(elementInSet) += addOrSubtract, s2)
else
(s1, s2(elementInSet) += addOrSubtract)
  }

 // If the new solution is better, accept it, else compute acceptance probability
  def acceptanceProbability(energies:(Double,Double), temperature:Double) = {
    val diff = energies._1 - energies._2
    if (diff < 0 ) 1.0 else math.exp(diff/temperature)
  }

  def compute( best:Seq[City], temp:Double):Seq[City] = {
    if (temp > 1) {
          val newSolution = createNeighbour( best )
          val currentEnergy = length(best)
          val neighbourEnergy = length(newSolution)

          // Decide if we should accept the neighbour
          val accept = (acceptanceProbability((currentEnergy, neighbourEnergy), temp) > math.random) &&
                       (length(newSolution) < length(best))
          compute( if (accept) {
                    printf("\nLength: %.2f, Temperature: %.2f", length(newSolution), temp)
                    newSolution
                  } else best, (1-coolingRate)*temp)
    } else best
  }

object ponder {

  def listOfInts(minel: Int, maxel: Int, n: Int, k: Int): Stream[List[Int]] = {
    if (k == n)
      Stream(List())
    else {
      val a = for {
        i <- (minel + 1) to (maxel - (n - k) + 1)
        row <- listOfInts(i, maxel, n, k + 1)
      } yield i :: row
      a.toStream
    }
  }                                               //> listOfInts: (minel: Int, maxel: Int, n: Int, k: Int)Stream[List[Int]]
  
  
  def listOfInts2(minel: Int, maxel: Int, n: Int, k: Int): Stream[List[Int]] = {
    if (k == n)
      Stream(List())
    else {
      val a = for {
        i <- (minel + 1) to (minel + 11)
        row <- listOfInts2(i, maxel, n, k + 1)
      } yield i :: row
      a.toStream
    }
  }                                               //> listOfInts2: (minel: Int, maxel: Int, n: Int, k: Int)Stream[List[Int]]
    
  //  val S1Stream = listOfInts(0, 13, 6, 0)
  //  val S2Stream = listOfInts(0, 23, 6, 0)

  
val S1Stream = listOfInts2(1,15,5,0)              //> S1Stream  : Stream[List[Int]] = Stream(List(2, 3, 4, 5, 6), ?)
val S2Stream = listOfInts2(2, 15,5,0)             //> S2Stream  : Stream[List[Int]] = Stream(List(3, 4, 5, 6, 7), ?)

  val (initialTemperature, coolingRate) = (2.0, 0.001)
                                                  //> initialTemperature  : Double = 2.0
                                                  //| coolingRate  : Double = 0.001

  case class City(x: Int, y: Int)

  def distance(a: City, b: City) = math.sqrt(List((a.x - b.x), (a.y - b.y)).map(x => x * x).sum)
                                                  //> distance: (a: ponder.City, b: ponder.City)Double

  def mkTour(tour: Seq[City]) = {
    val (i, j) = (util.Random.nextInt(tour.size), util.Random.nextInt(tour.size))
    tour
      .patch(i, Seq(tour(j)), 1)
      .patch(j, Seq(tour(i)), 1)
  }                                               //> mkTour: (tour: Seq[ponder.City])Seq[ponder.City]

  def length(tour: Seq[City]) = tour.foldLeft(0.0, tour.head)((a, b) => (a._1 + distance(a._2, b), b))._1
                                                  //> length: (tour: Seq[ponder.City])Double

  def createNeighbour(s1: List[Int], s2: List[Int]) = {
    val r = util.Random.nextInt(24)
    //0 to 11 are subtract
    //12 to 23 are add
    val addOrSubtract = 2 * (r / 12) - 1

    //000000,111111,222222,333333...
    val set1or2 = (r / 6) % 2

    val elementInSet = r % 6

    if (set1or2 == 1)
      (s1.updated(elementInSet, s1(elementInSet) + addOrSubtract), s2)
    else
      (s1, s2.updated(elementInSet, s2(elementInSet) + addOrSubtract))
  }                                               //> createNeighbour: (s1: List[Int], s2: List[Int])(List[Int], List[Int])


def numRemainedrs(S1: List[Int], S2: List[Int]) =
{
      val products = (for {
        s1 <- S1
        s2 <- S2
      } yield (s1 * s2)).toSet

      val coveringSet = products ++ (products map (_ + 1)) ++ (products map (_ - 1))
    val remainders = (1 to 59).toSet -- coveringSet
		remainders.size
}                                                 //> numRemainedrs: (S1: List[Int], S2: List[Int])Int


  def largestRun(S1: List[Int], S2: List[Int]) =
    {
      val products = (for {
        s1 <- S1
        s2 <- S2
      } yield (s1 * s2)).toSet

      val coveringSet = products ++ (products map (_ + 1)) ++ (products map (_ - 1))

      val coveringList = coveringSet.toList.sorted
if (coveringList.head == 1) {
      val d = coveringList.sliding(2).toList indexWhere { case List(a, b) => b > a + 1 }
      if (d == -1)
      coveringList.last
      else
      coveringList(d)
      }
      else
      0
      /*val diffs = coveringList.tail zip( coveringList drop 1)
	val diffs2 = diffs map (x=> x._1 - x._2)
	diffs2 indexWhere(_ > 1)*/

    }                                             //> largestRun: (S1: List[Int], S2: List[Int])Int

  // If the new solution is better, accept it, else compute acceptance probability
  def acceptanceProbability(oldEnergy: Double, newEnergy: Double, temperature: Double) = {
    math.exp(  (oldEnergy - newEnergy) / temperature)
  }                                               //> acceptanceProbability: (oldEnergy: Double, newEnergy: Double, temperature: 
                                                  //| Double)Double

  def compute(bestS1: List[Int], bestS2: List[Int], temp: Double): (List[Int], List[Int]) = {
    if (temp > .00001) {
      val newSolution = createNeighbour(bestS1, bestS2)
    //  println("NewSolution", newSolution._1, newSolution._2)
      val currentEnergy = numRemainedrs(bestS1, bestS2)
//      val currentEnergy = largestRun(bestS1, bestS2)
    //  println("currentEnergy", currentEnergy)
  
  val neighbourEnergy = numRemainedrs(newSolution._1, newSolution._2)
  //    val neighbourEnergy = largestRun(newSolution._1, newSolution._2)
    //if (neighbourEnergy > 56)
    if (neighbourEnergy == 0 )
    { println("neighbourEnergy", neighbourEnergy, newSolution._1, newSolution._2 ) }
      // Decide if we should accept the neighbour
      val acceptProb = acceptanceProbability(currentEnergy, neighbourEnergy, temp)
    //  println("accept prob", acceptProb)
      val accept = (acceptProb> math.random) /*&&
                       (length(newSolution) < length(best))*/
      if (accept) {
    //    println("Accepted Energy: ", neighbourEnergy, "Temperature: ", temp)
        compute(newSolution._1, newSolution._2, (1 - coolingRate) * temp)
      } else {
    //  println("Did not accepted Energy: ", neighbourEnergy, "Temperature: ", temp)
      compute(bestS1, bestS2, (1 - coolingRate) * temp)
      }
    } else (bestS1, bestS2)
  }                                               //> compute: (bestS1: List[Int], bestS2: List[Int], temp: Double)(List[Int], Li
                                                  //| st[Int])

  def main(args: Array[String]) = {
    for (iii <- 1 to 10000) {
      val best = compute(List(1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6), List(2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7), initialTemperature)
      val bestRun = numRemainedrs(best._1, best._2)
      if (bestRun <= 3) {
        println("Final solution", bestRun)
        println("Tour: " + best._1.sorted + best._2.sorted)
      }
    }
  }                                               //> main: (args: Array[String])Unit

  main(Array())                                   //> (Final solution,3)

r((1 to 60) map covers, Set(), Set())          //> res8: Boolean = false

  def r(c: IndexedSeq[List[(Int, Int)]], S1: Set[Int], S2: Set[Int]): Boolean = {
    if (S1.size > 6 || S2.size > 6)
      false
    else if (c isEmpty) {
      println("Solution found!")
      println(S1.toList.sorted)
      println(S2.toList.sorted)
      true
    } else {
      // 4 cases
      // s1 is/isn't in S1
      // s2 is/isn't in S2
    
    // Start with the ones that don't add anything to the sets
    val cParted = c partition(x => x exists(y => S1.contains(y._1) && S2.contains(y._2)))
    
    
      val cSorted = cParted._2 sortWith (_.length < _.length)
      if (cSorted.isEmpty)
      r(cSorted,S1,S2)
      else
 //     c.head exists (ses => r(c.tail, S1 + ses._1, S2 + ses._2))
     cSorted.head exists (ses => r(cSorted.tail, S1 + ses._1, S2 + ses._2))
    }
  }


r((1 to 58) map covers, Set(), Set())          //> res8: Boolean = false


r((1 to 57) map covers, Set(), Set())          //> Solution found!

                                                  //| res8: Boolean = true
